RATING: 8.6
Replayability is really good even if you play with the same people all the time. When you play with different people each time it varies since some people might be attracted to smuggling, others maybe they're terrible liars - you'll have fun figuring out how people play. 
When you play with the same people time after time, things can get very interesting since you may say things like "The last few games Molly never lied, I'll just let her through" then lo and behold her entire bag was filled with contraband!!

And then the Quality is fantastic. Absolutely nothing to complain about! I would even recommend using the app as it adds great background noises during the timer, and a very attractive final score reveal!

All in all, this is a great bluffing game with lots of little tricks to think about. Trying to trick the sheriff, or find the tricksters when you are the sheriff, it's all great fun! It's almost like you should "Play the Sheriff, not the game." - but the game itself is actually pretty clever too. Trying to get the most apples or bread than your opponents is challenging. I really enjoy how all the points add up in the end - reminds me a bit like 7 Wonders scoring!

I would definitely recommend!

RATING: 9
[COLOR=#FFFFFF][BGCOLOR=#FF9933][b]aaj's FAVORITE BLUFFING GAME[/b][/BGCOLOR][/COLOR]
[i]tl;dr - This is my favorite social game that actually hides a really good game behind itself. I love the bluffing aspect, and this always is welcome at our table. 10/10, highly recommended.[/i]
[COLOR=#CCCCFF]____________________________[/COLOR]

One of our very favorites. In Sheriff of Nottingham, each player plays as a merchant, who is trying to bring goods to market under the nose of the powerful Sheriff of Nottingham. Players take turns in the role of the sheriff, and must try to guess what other players are bringing in: legal goods, or valuable contraband pepper, silk, and mead? The player with the most valuable market at the end of the game wins!

Sheriff is a different game with every different group you play with, and the role of Sheriff is never safe from crushing loss or lots of gain. We love this game and the bluffing that it provokes from cocky smugglers and honest merchants alike. 

This game is exponentially more fun the more you get into the sheriff/merchant roleplaying. Recently we had a friend who responded to every question from the sheriff with the same smarmy, "Yes/No your Lordship." and "Just a humble merchant, your Lordship." We've also had blustering Sheriffs, timid Sheriffs, and loose cannon Sheriffs that will sometimes open every bag and sometimes let everything pass scot-free. Great fun!

Sheriff of Nottingham really gets people out of their comfort zone in a competitive, but not overly-complicated game. It has great replayability because it doesn't rely on new cards or greater difficulties to stay fresh, but instead changes based on the moods and strategies of the players around the table.

RATING: 6
Fun game, but a lot of the victory is reliant on luck of the draw. There seems to be nothing you can do to stop a player from playing honestly and that particular strategy wins games more often than not. The contraband is only worth so much, and to beat the bonuses from the King and Queen end-game point boosts, you need a LOT of contraband. Even players mixing the two strategies win games less often than players going 100% honest. There needs to be some downside to only putting honest goods in your bag, because right now, I could draw 5 Chickens, put them in the bag, and practically win the King's Bonus. There is also no incentive for the player to bribe the Sheriff, so there's no down-side to not giving the Sheriff any money at all and reaping huge benefits anyways.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A game I regrettably haven't played enough of. Or have I? I don't know, maybe I'm bluffing. Actually, I really haven't. Seriously. I want to play this more. Or maybe I'm bluffing again. You'll have to open the bag to really find out.

Sheriff of Nottingham preys upon our curiosity. From the outside looking in, you might think that the pressure is on the merchants to try and sneak some goods through the Sheriff and into their stall/contraband pile. And, for sure, there is pressure on them to do so. But it's really the Sheriff who has to think carefully in all of this. The impulse is just to see what is in the bag. Will the curiosity get the better of the Sheriff or will it be the undoing of the merchant?

It's this sort of free-form negotiation and social deduction that makes Sheriff so fun. The ever-changing landscape of goods and money creates an atmosphere that goes above and beyond any final scoring. In fact, the scoring structure just lends a bit of foundation for what is really just an incredibly fun social activity.

RATING: 7.5
The artwork and quality of tiles and coins in this game is top-notch. The plastic button snaps on the plastic/velvet bags suck. We had to abstain from snapping/unsnapping bags (even though the rules encourage it from a signal-of-intent perspective) for fear that we would either rip a hole in the bags or the snaps out of the bags. 

The free app is excellent and adds some great sound effects and Monty Python-esque humor to the proceedings. It also can handle all the MATH required at the end to add up your points. For a game so light and fluffy, the avalanche of math that falls on you at the end to determine winners is a pain. The app lightens this burden.

I had grand hopes of my fun loving, jovial gaming group hopping right into role playing this game, as so many others have said... but something about it caused them not to. It was a very dry, "I have five apples," experience. We didn't need a timer at all we were whipping through rounds so fast. Interestingly, everyone said it was fun, but it wasn't the instant-fun-maker other folks have referred to in their reviews. I still like the game, but maybe I need to find a theater troupe to play it with.

Positives
- Fantastic artwork, quality tiles and coins
- Excellent companion app
- Simple mechanics
- Encourages role-playing

Negatives
- Bags look awesome on the surface, but their cheap quality manifests the first time you try to unsnap them
- Easy to sidestep role-playing and make gameplay very perfunctory and dry
- For such a simple concept, the rulebook is dense with text, technicalities and examples-- which can be good and bad
- Final scoring is very complex in comparison to the game mechanics

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
With the right group this is a really fun game!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I played this game just once, so these are mostly impressions that may change after multiple plays.

Even if I'm very bad at bluffing, I really think that Sheriff of Nottingham is one of the best games out there for social play. The key of this success is its mix of bluffing and negotiation, which brings out many jokes, discussions, role-playing and so on. It just works really well for that. Yet what makes me enjoy this game even more is the fact that, unlike other bluffing games, there's actually a game beneath all the lying... even if that game is just plain simple set collection. Also is worth mentioning that this game has gorgeous artwork and high quality components. Everything is just really pleasing to watch. 

I would like to give it a higher ranking, but I do have one problem with this game... well, me! The fact that I'm so bad at bluffing and negotiation brings me quite often at making a fool of myself. I know I shouldn't let this fact influence my opinion of the design... but the truth is: even if I'll have fun playing this game, I'll constantly show everybody just how pathetic I'm at bluffing and negotiating. 

Overall a very well put together game, that will probably never fail to create social interactions between the players at the table... I just wish I was a little better at it to be able to enjoy it more.

RATING: 7
In Sheriff of Nottingham, players will not only be able to experience Nottingham as a merchant of the city, but each turn one player will step into the shoes of the Sheriff himself. Players declare goods they wish to bring into the city, goods that are secretly stored in their burlap sack. The Sheriff must then determine who gets into the city with their goods, who gets inspected, and who may have their goods confiscated!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In general, I don't care a lot for strict negotiation games. But the gameplay in Nottingham is fairly novel. It has a certain charm I like. There's quite a bit of intriguing gameplay in figuring out how / when to bluff or make deals. It's neat, fast, and fun.

RATING: 5
This is a smuggling goods (cards) past an inspector (rotating from player to player) kind of game, and as such, is dominated by determining when to lie...and when the other players are lying, or telling the truth, about the cards they have secretly placed in their envelopes. On the plus side, the game creates a lot of table talk, and the joy, I suppose, of catching other players when the lie (but not you when you lie). 

On the minus side, the game, turn in and turn out, essentially teaches and rewards lying and getting away with it (best approach), as opposed to lying and getting caught (not as good, but still not too bad) and telling the truth (which might be a decent strategy, but definitely NOT the point of playing this particular game).  

One plays this particular game to enjoy lying and getting away with it, and making lots of money when you do lie.  Hmmmm...I wonder what this game is implicitly teaching its players?  This game straightforwardly fails my "the world would be a worse place if more people played this game test," and so I definitely cannot recommend it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
While not the most original bluffing/deduction game, it manages to do 3 things very well. First, the art-work and theme makes sense and adds to the overall experience. Secondly, the negotiation rules are well-defined and add mechanics (snapping of the bag) that eliminate any ambiguity or "slow-rolling" a player may do, in order to bend the rules into his/her favor. And finally, the fact that contraband cards are placed above a player creates useful information so players can see how truthful they have been in pass rounds. 

That being said, the game doesn't provide much useful/concrete information to make decisions. In other words, one's intuition/gut-feeling is going to be the driving force behind any decision. As an ice-breaker party game with new players, I like the game quite a bit. But with the same group, it may get tiresome over time.

Component quality was iffy. I love the art work and cardboard components. Unfortunately, it didn't take half a game for one of the merchant bags to rip.

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Sheriff of Nottingham is a simple bluffing game: each turn one player is the Sheriff, and other players try to bring goods (legal or contraband) inside the city.

Merchants declare one type of legal good, but can put anything inside their little velvety bags... The Sheriff can decide to let them pass (usually if they are "generous" to him...) or to inspect the bags. If the bag is opened by the Sheriff, goods not declared are discarded and a fine must be paid; but if the merchant did a rightful declaration, the Sheriff is the one who pays.

There is lot of ways one can negotiate, bluff and smuggle. A sort of poker-like metagame thrives since the first turns. And the game is quite enjoyable, even by non-gamers (and even by me, not overly fond of the bluff and not remotely good at bluffing).

Sheriff is a quite good game, and fills a niche not covered by anything else in my collection.

RATING: N/A
1249
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This social bluffing game requires just enough tact using its mechanisms that I wouldn't consider it a party game, but is quick enough to learn and easy enough to understand the strategy of to be entry level and entertaining for varying ages. In a nut shell, you take turns being the sheriff and deciding who's goods will pass unchecked and who's will be inspected. The catch is that the goods checked will either reward the sheriff of contraband is found, or penalize the sheriff if the person is being honest. 

One of the unique things about this game is that it's a bluffing game, but choosing to never lie is a completely legitimate strategy, and I've seen people win simply because they didn't lie until the very last round, and pushed 5 contraband in all at once. 

Highly recommend you try this one, espescially if playing with people who will get into the theme and act a bit.

RATING: 7
Simple and fun game all about lying, bluffing, extortion, and bribery. Of course it's going to be fun

Each player takes turns being the Sheriff and every other player tries to put goods in their bag to take to the market. The Sheriff gets to choose to inspect each bag, if there are illegal goods they get confiscated and the offender must pay a fine, but if it's legitimate the Sheriff must pay the fine. The trick is, you can bribe the Sheriff to not check your bag. This leads to a wonderful, unique game all about extorting and trying to double bluff people. 

Tutorial: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ofZS29XArzM

RATING: 8
This game is really fun and typically hilarious, even more so if you're playing with interesting people, but there's two problems that might arise after multiple play throughs:
1) If you're playing with the same people over and over, you'll become so accustom to the way they barter and bluff that the game gets extremely repetitive. So recruiting interesting people to play with is crucial, because you need people that can regularly switch up their bluffing tactics.
2) Even if you are able to regularly switch up your bluffing tactics, there always comes a point where your group can predict how you'll act in any given situation. It's near impossible to play this game with the same group of people without it eventually getting repetitive, there's no way to get around the fact that this game will get repetitive if you're not playing with multiple different groups of people.

Otherwise, this is an excellent game, albeit, one with limited replay value.

RATING: 8.75
Fantastic bluffing game.

Being the sheriff is more stressful than I thought it would be and I love either trying to sneak in contraband or get the sheriff to open a bag of full of legitimate goods. 

Sheriff of Nottingham takes the best part of bluffing games (looking each other in the eye and trying to deduce if the other person is lying or not) and makes that 75% of what you do in the game.

All that and a near perfect production make this one of the top bluffing games out there.

The only downside is that it can drag if people don't keep things moving.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The Draw-Phase (refilling hands) combined with the way the discard piles are treated kills the pacing of the game. The way the Sheriff must remember every kind of visible card the players pick up is a bit gamey and annoying. 

There's been a lot of discussion whether Honest play is unbalanced. According to my experience it is, or at least, it incentivizes people from taking risks, which is a shame because it reduces the chaotic atmosphere. And don't even mention the bonus point counting. It's just tedious beyond belief. I don't want to spend minutes comparing cards back and forth with everyone for the game to end, I want to play again!

I might try the Zee-Garcia-variant where there is only one face down discard pile, no end-game bonuses, no drawing from discard pile and a 6 or 7 card hand limit. It should encourage (and force) players to take more risks and raise the stakes for bribing.

RATING: 4
Maybe the most repetitive game I have ever played. An hour of doing the same thing over and over again. And the winner comes down to a spreadsheet scoring exercise. 

To me, it is basically broken that it can easily be won without ever taking risk, or very little. It needs the players to play badly for the fun to creep in. 

Bluffing games need for there to be some logic to be applied. A game like poker is basically a big logic puzzle. This game is just guesswork. It isn't a horrible game to play, but endless better games in its niche.

RATING: 5
A pure bluffing game where all you are trying to do is get sets of goods past the sheriff while trying to sneak contraband as they score many more points than the regular goods. The sheriff goes around the table twice and that's the game. Scoring is based on goods successfully passed by the sheriff and bonus points for having the most in each set. My problem is the game is entirely too long 75 minutes for a 5-player game where you do the same thing in round 1 as round 10 just makes it drag. Part of that is because I am not a huge fan of bluffing, but I do enjoy it in quicker games like Bang: Dice or Incan Gold. Glad I got to play it, but not one I'm eager to play again.

RATING: 7.5
Fun and entertaining. The rules are a simple set up for the bluff, which is where the game really shines. Although you can easily play it straight, and earn a respectable score, the game is well-balanced to tempt you with the extra easy coin you get pick up from smuggling - assuming you get away with it of course.
The game really benefits by laying some ground rules for the bluff/bribe stage and then leaving the rest up to you. The simple mechanic of having your cards in pouches make it clear when a bribe has been accepted or not and helps avoid any arguments.
I played this with my wife and young daughters and it works well as a fun family game which we all enjoyed. I definitely get the impression that 4 or 5 players are better than 3.

RATING: 8
I really enjoyed this bluffing game.  Bluffing is a mechanism that I really enjoy and it is at the heart of this game.  You try to get contraband goods past the Sheriff and all players get a turn at being the Sheriff twice during the game.

My only complaint is that playing it safe 100% of the time seems to be a bit too strong of a strategy, but maybe that's an issue more with my group than the game itself.  I would rate this a bit higher, but the game does seem to take a tad too long for what it delivers.  Liar's Dice can provide a similar thrill in a fraction of the time.  There will still be a place for this on my shelf, though, as the theme this delivers over a game like Liar's makes it worthy enough to hit the table every now and then.

RATING: 7
Before heading to a game night, one of my friends said "I'm really in a mood to play a bluffing game where a rich dude is exploiting other people for their money." I knew what I had to do.

Sheriff is ridiculous. My sister pretty much always beats me by playing it completely straight the whole game. I've heard this is a common winning strategy, and that seems to go against what the game is trying to be. But otherwise it's just pure theater, which could be what you're looking for in between bigger games.

That said, I don't think it's the best social game ever made (that title currently goes to Coup), and I've found it gets stale pretty quickly. Still, it's an entertaining thing that can show people what modern board gaming can be all about.

RATING: 7
n Sheriff of Nottingham, you live the high glamorous life of a customs agent, patrolling the borders of Nottingham seeking contraband that might be sold on the open market.  Sure, he may say he's a harmless chicken farmer, but those bags aren't exactly moving and clucking all that much.  But you might be convinced to not take a peek... for a fee.

Interesting Mechanic: bribery.  Sheriff of Nottingham is, at it's core, a game about lying, bribery and mutual understandings, wink wink nudge nudge.  You fill a bag with goods and declare the contents of them, and pass them to the current Sheriff.  The Sheriff then decides whether or not your bags merit closer inspection, and that decision might be made easier with a donation to local law enforcement, which is woefully underfunded by an underappreciative public.  If he looks and you have contraband, you're in trouble, but the penalties are staggering if his instincts are wrong.  But don't get too cocky - eventually you will take your turn as the Sheriff.

Sheriff of Nottingham is, at it's core, a social game, and is far better in a group that is extroverted, silly and familiar with each other.  It is a tad prone to lucky streaks - a player can get so lucky drawing goods that he rarely or never needs to lie - but this is a relatively quick game where the experience is generally more valuable than winning or losing anyway.

RATING: 7
Thus far, my favorite "lie your lying face off" (aka "bluffing") game I've found. Not a genre I enjoy playing too much - I find them slightly stressful - but it can be fun once in a while. The incentives in this one are really nicely balanced to incentivize deception, bluffing, and negotiation with a lovely imbalance: one side has all the information, the other side *may* have all the power.

Seems to naturally encourage a light touch of roleplaying and just the right sort of light-hearted grudges and vendettas - whenever the sheriff searches, someone gets burned.

Highly recommend playing with an N-minute timer on the bargaining round. Moderately recommend some sort of convention as to whether each search is happening (we used "is the snap on a pouch open at the moment the timer runs out?")

RATING: 6
No real complaints about this game, given what it is. I think in awhile its score will drop to 5, but for now I think a 6 is fair.

The game is light, and without the sort of strategy I enjoy to my highest rated games. I like face to face challenge, and having to be social in games in order to pull off a win, but I also like having some system or possible deeper strategy that allows for trumping any opposition at certain times in a game if you set yourself up right. This was a pretty much straight up bluff game in which you sort of pattern analyze your stakes, gauge your lead (or amount you are behind) versus the player who is the sheriff and secondarily the other players.

This is just light fun. It doesn't overstay its welcome- game length is good. Scoring is interestingly complex at the end, but in thinking about it, it is a fitting system for the game and helps it to feel fair when all is said and done.

No real criticisms to take away points, no real "wow" parts to add extra. So, there ya go.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Sheriff of Nottingham is a game I enjoy because I am a fan of bluffing games, and Sheriff of Nottingham is a game that presents a platform for bluffing that is very unique.

The conceit of the game is straightforward and quick to pick up after a round or two, but the core of the game comes during the exchange between Sheriff and Trader. Initially, it seems almost basic - the trader must try to smuggle in contraband, and the sheriff must decide if they'll accept bribes or promises to turn a blind eye. What gives the game depth is the fact that bringing in nothing but legitimate goods means that a Sheriff who searches your bag must pay a penalty. This lends depth to the amount of moves a player can make, and leads to hilarious "you think that I think that YOU think" moments as players try to untangle each others' motives.

There are a couple of shortcomings, unfortunately. One is that score is not easily determined or kept during the game, and instead must be sorted out at the end of the game with pens and paper. While this is true of a lot of games, Sheriff of Nottingham is a bit egregious - I've once seen a game take 20 minutes to calculate with inexperienced players. The other is that the game itself tends to run out of steam near the end; the gameplay doesn't really change up at any point, so if you don't enjoy the core loop, you're going to find this a drag.

Overall though, I've greatly enjoyed my time with Sheriff of Nottingham, and I would recommend it to anyone enjoys bluffing and deception

RATING: 6.75
Rated after 3 plays @ 5 players

The game is easy to explain and doesn't take much to get started. Make sure to follow the 1 min timer per player on the sheriff to keep the game moving and don't forget there are plenty of ways other than money to make a bribe. I found that going with the honest strategy worked pretty well in the first game. By the third, the honest strategy wasn't earning enough money so I needed to take more risks with contraband.

I would play again but the game really needs the higher player count (4 or 5) to work. Less than that and it loses some of the chaos and dynamics that make it fun.

RATING: 6.2
[May 2015 - 6.2]
I'm finding this one to be a little too random and loose and like The Resistance, the bluffing gets a little old after awhile. 

[March 2015 - 7]
I was at the grocery the other day and got some donuts in a bag, did my other shopping and went to checkout line where the lady asked me what was in the bag to ring it up. I had to pause and think a minute -- "uh, five donuts," which was true. I laughed to myself as it reminded me of this game, when you have that moment of "oh crap, what's in my bag" -- the pause can sometimes give away a lie ... or a bluff.

This is a fun party game. Everyone gets it and enjoys it, it moves along quickly, etc. There's also some strategy and player interaction for the race to the top of the items. That, in itself, adds a layer to the game to keep it from being "meh" to "okay, I have to pay attention here and make it a race."

RATING: 8
Once you see the merchants, you're curious. Once you see the contraband you're engaged. Once you see the bags, your sold. 

Every time I've taught Nottingham, it comes to life.

And importantly, Nottingham works because it is inherently human! This isn't a game where I have to explain that "it's so cool because the interface of abstract systems all make a rich and compelling puzzle." No! Nottingham does that with first impressions! 

There's inherit joy in the actions of the game. We want to open up the bag and see whats inside. We want to accept bribes. We want to lie to our friends in the open and get away with it. 

We want to be together and screw each other over. It's beautiful, and I can play it with anyone.

RATING: 8
I am constantly disappointed in my game group for not finding the fun in this game, as I always have a blast with it. It's been said in many reviews, but the feeling of having the current sheriff holding your bag of goods as you attempt to negotiate a deal, only to have him snap it open at the end, is excellent.

To those who claim that it's 'always better to tell the truth,' I would argue this is expressly false for your group, if that's the agreed mindset. If everyone believes that the smartest option is to tell the truth, then it's that much easier to get prohibited goods through. The mindset will encourage the playing of the other mindset.

RATING: 7
Sheriff of Nottingham is a great example of gaming as Entertainment. You have some items and you want to get them through 'customs'. You lie and negotiate with the Sheriff so that you get stuff through, or he searches you and you pay a fine.

That is about it. The scoring is a rather annoying fiddley thing based around set collecting, and it sits at odds with the rather free-flowing neotiation game. It is also a little long for a light game.

And there does seem to be an easy option of simply telling the truth at all times. This negates the negotiation aspect of the game and does seem to produce a winning formula. And the game falls a little flat without negotiation and bluffing.

So if you and the rest of your group like table-talk, and negotiation games with the chance to lie and bluff your way through, then this will work well.

RATING: N/A
諾丁漢警長
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.75
This is a bluffing game that is somewhat similar to the card game BS or Liar's Dice.  It's a bit more complex and has more layers than either of those.  

Players take turns being the Sheriff and all of the other players hands him/her a bag full of goods.  The players all declare what they have in the bag and it is up to the Sheriff to decide if they wish to inspect it.  If an inspected bag contains contraband there are fines to be paid; likewise if an inspected bag matched what was declared, the Sheriff must pay a penalty.  Players are free to wheel and deal and bribe the Sheriff to allow their bags to pass.  

The is a fun bluffing game full of mind games and reverse psychology.  Of course, you can always choose to play it honestly, but it isn't always the best policy.  

A minor quibble is that the end game scoring can be a little work.  However, this does not detract from the fun of the game itself.  The game plays with a minimum of 3, but definitely seems more fun with 4 or 5.  Recommended!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
A renamed and available in UK version of Robin Hood.... might actually be able to get my hands on it then.
I have already purchased a copy... now eagerly awaiting October when it will actually arrive :)

Yay!

It finally arrived, after pre-ordering with my FLGS in August, this finally arrived.

I am so excited by this neat little bluffing, set collection game I cant wait to give it a go.

I didn't get my pre-order promo :soblue:

Really really enjoyed this neat little bluffing game, I left the promo pack at home :blush:. so we stripped out the royal bonus cards too and played the base game with no frills. 

I really really enjoyed it. The dual discard piles make for a very interesting card draw mechanic however the contraband cards in said discard piles quickly make it difficult to draw thus you tend to draw blind, which in turn makes it harder for the sheriff to detect your bluffs as he has no idea what you drew.

Whilst I did enjoy this with thee player I think it will really shine with the full compliment of five players and I hope it will become a staple of our game group.
The only complaint I have, and it is a little niggle is that the little market goods bags are very stiff to open and close and I am concerned that the popper will actually tear free of the bag and then I will cry :cry:

RATING: 7.5
Pros
-Somewhat promotes role playing
-Flexible bluffing fun
-Lots of variety of goods
-Players have lots of options and choices on what to do on their turn / how they want to play 

Cons
-Telling truth seems too viable, undermines the lying aspect of the game
-Illegal goods seem underwhelming
-Only one resource limits degree of negotiation/trade available
-Bribing feels very mathy (calculating profit etc)
-Deciding whether or not if someone is lying feels very much like just guessing, despite having some information, there isn't very many tells.

RATING: 6
Sheriff of Nottingham is basically a pimped edition of the old game Contraband, with players trying to smuggle stuff past the Sheriff (in this case) with him being (more or less) fully aware that he's being duped but getting his cut. A pure bluffing game, in other words. Improvements over the old incarnation include upgraded components and a shorter playtime, but I still think it takes a bit too long. For a pure bluffing game, it's bloddy hard to beat out something so simple as Cockroach Poker. All the added fluff basically just extends the playtime without adding much to the game.

RATING: 4
To me, this game is broken. There is so little incentive to try and sneak contraband (reward/risk ratio is just too low). They should be worth more coins or there should be a king and queen of contraband.
You are trying to get 8 coins worth of illegal goods through? Simply bribe the Sheriff and give him 3 or 4 coins. But why not just get 4 coins worth of legal goods through then ? You'd get even more if the Sheriff opens your bag and it builds towards the king and queen rewards.
In my opinion, this game does not reward bluff enough and games can get dry as the group quickly becomes a bunch of honest merchants passing honest goods. Not that fun if you ask me. But who am I to say..

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
First play. I was skeptical at first, but was quickly won over, and in fact laughed as hard as I have laughed in years. I tend to be skeptical of hype, but this game is a winner with us (a casual/social group), and for a good price.

Kind of a distilled bluffing game--you'll need to work on a game face here, and it's good to get into character. "Hello sheriff, I have some apples here to bake two pies for my mum." Some of the deals people make feel a little broken to me--if you let me through this time, I'll let you through next time--but all in all, we're happy to pull this one out from time to time. It's not something you'd want to play too frequently.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
My daughter received this from a friend for her birthday, so we borrowed it from a friend first to see if she would like it.  I played it first with my lunchtime game group (with some of the rule details wrong), and enjoyed it.  

Played it last night with my wife and two oldest kids.  The younger, almost 8, took a few rounds to understand what he was supposed to be doing, and made some ... interesting decisions ("I'm always going to open every bag."  "I'll give you 20 gold not to open my bag"), but he thought it was a blast, and somehow ended up in 1st or 2nd place for all of the goods.  My daughter was very conservative (usually only taking 1 or 2 goods), but wanted to play another round to try being sneaky.  She was doing well until she gave away that 20 gold that she'd just received...and lost by a point to my wife.  It was a very different experience, but a lot of fun.  She liked it enough to keep it, and any game that those two kids will play together (for now at least) is a winner in my book.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
As with Betrayal at House on the Hill, I really want to like this game. Unlike BaHotH though, this time it's more my fault rather then the games issues holding it back.

My biggest problem with Sherrif of Nottingham is that I'm quite bad at bluffing. At first I tried to role-play this game but that really fell pretty flat with the different people I played with. Most of the time people had more success by trying a Euro approach, offering a reasonable amount to pass illegal goods. This approach still didn't work for me though. Probably because I'm too easy to read and people just opened my bag when I tried to bribe them. 

The game doesn't have a catch-up mechanic (aside from going big on contraband) and the theme is pretty thin. Because of this I didn't have that much fun when I was losing. Essentially the drier this game gets (more emphasis on calculation rather then flamboyant deception) the more annoyed I got when I fell behind.

The game has an insert (hooray!) but some of the components are a bit meh. The Sherrif standee showed signs of wear and tear after the first game. More problematic is that people didn't dare opening the bags out of fear or ripping them apart. The snapping sound is cool but pointless if people just leave the flap down without actually closing the bag.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A fun bluffing game. Might do better in a 5-player game if everyone only were sheriff once.

The last player in the circle has a different dynamic to contend with, which is that everyone else is more inclined to 'go big or go home' with their bluffs because the game-end is coming right up. Of course, that creates opportunity, too, for negotiation.

Negotiation is interesting. Our group used mostly gold at first—and then I forced a transition to using inventory in the bag and then planning for that by stuffing my bag with contraband, thinking I would give some of it away to the sheriff.

Might actually be a lot of fun to try again.

RATING: 8
This is the exact kind of game I love to play. It's essentially of gateway weight, and yet it is nasty enough that only certain gamers will really get into it. This is a game almost entirely of bluffing and psychology, with just a dash of tactical play. Outwitting an opponent entirely feels great. GETTING outwitted entirely, not so much. Personally, I live for the moments of "being outwitted" as well, but I can see why people might think this game just makes them feel stupid. Others complain that the bartering process takes too long (or needs to be restricted with a timer) when, in my mind, there's no such thing as too long of a bartering session. As I said, this game is exactly for people like me: liars.

RATING: 7
*起始形成兩疊各五張的棄牌推，每個人50圓，六張牌
*三人9輪，四人以上，人數*2輪
*每輪五個階段，每個階段每個人輪流做事
A 市場，蓋著最多五張牌在旁邊，然後補牌到六張，一定要先抽棄牌推，才能抽牌庫，棄牌推要照順序抽，將蓋著的牌一起放到某個棄牌推，順序隨便
B 放牌到袋中，一到五張
C 宣告你袋中貨物，只能宣告一種合法貨物，張數要對
D 警長審查，可用各種貨物賄絡(錢，送完的卡，袋中物品，未來承諾)，過的話，合法卡打開放置，違禁品蓋著放上面，如果檢視，你說實話警長要陪你懲罰的錢，說謊的話，有說的合法貨物依舊得到，違法或沒說的警長選棄牌推丟，你要付罰鍰給警長
E 補手牌到六張
*卡牌全用完則除了棄牌推上面五張，其它重洗
*最後記分可以先記物品擁有最多的第一第二額外分數，在各別記所有物品分數跟錢
*變體 手牌上限七張，起始移掉10張牌

RATING: 8
Use the Merry Men expansion, it`s a must...

Base Sheriff of Nottingham is an OK bluffing game, but saying the truth is too overpowered. People could easily win the game just saying the truth, if you don`t believe it, try it, but with the Merry Men expansion, maaan it`s a different story. You must try lying, since you could get a really huge amounts of money for that. Forget the 6-9 gold worth contrabands from the base game, I`m talking about the ~30 gold worth black market cards, so people have to lie a few time just to stop people for getting them.

Alfre
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
After seeing this game featured on the youtube TableTop show, we knew it was the next game to add to our collection. 

It's very easy to pick up after watching the show, and relatively easy to teach, even to people who aren't familiar with more unique board games.

Most of the game components are decent quality. The cardboard market stands, sheriff, and coins are thick and durable, though when removing them from the packaging we had to be careful not to tear them.

We did have an issue with one of our market bags. It broke the day after we got it, because the snap was too strong for the fabric. However, I contacted the company and they responded within 24 hours and we had a brand new bag by the end of the week. Excellent customer service.

I would recommend this to pretty much anyone who enjoys a good game. It's easy to pick up, and the set time frame for the game also adds to it's appeal because you know you won't be stuck playing it forever.

RATING: 9
I'll come right out and say it.  This is THE game to own.  Sheriff of Nottingham is an absolute hit whenever I bring it out with friends.  

What this game offers is the ability to truly manipulate your experiance.  Going from being a merchant telling the truth, or lying to the sheriff and getting caught, can certainly alter the outcome causing some players to be overly suspiscious of you, and others may be trusting of you.  This game is simply a great game because the GAMEPLAY is where it excels more than anything.  Which is the most important part of the game, the gameplay.

The only issue I could possibly think of with this game is that there is no true play mat, instead there are small mats for each person individually.  However, I can understand why this system was used in place one of large play mat.  

Overall, 9/10 two thumbs up.

[b]A few different ideas for tricking the Sheriff:[/b]
Tell the Truth 
Straight Bluff
Double Bluff
Take discarded card Bluff
Promise goods you don't have in the sack Bluff
Promise the top card of contraband Bluff (keeping the lowest value on top)

[b]A few ideas for getting the most out of the merchants as Sheriff:[/b]
Open the bag with the smallest bribe on it.
2 bucks per item in the bag.

RATING: 10
This game is deception and deceit done right without having to take itself too seriously. I always enjoy popping this game out and introducing new people to it only for them to say at the end that they just bought the game online and plan to play it at home with their loved ones further increasing it's popularity. Now, what can I talk about Sheriff of Nottingham that hasn't already been said. From the calculating ways to trick the sheriff, the downright extortion the sheriff and players will do, and even the wonderful "SNAP" the poppers make, this game is loads of fun and is perfect for any board game night or get together. 

The only downside I have to say is the snappers on the bags. Plastic snappers don't snap easily as brass ones do. This causes the fabric to be tugged more harshly and could eventually lead to ripped bags trying to open those things. One alternative you can do is not snap the bags closed, but instead reach your hand in there pretending you are taking it out. However, if you pull the contents out it's like Popping the snapper open. 

Or, you can also contact Arcane Wonders if your bags have ripped and they will be so kind to replace them for you. Excellent game, excellent concept, and outstanding customer service. You can't go wrong with Sheriff of Nottingham from Arcane Wonders. It truly is deserving of the name Dice Tower Essential.

2014-09-05

Initial Rating: 6.5 (September 2014)

I was keen on trying another game from Arcane Wonders. I really liked it, perhaps it can go up in my personal ratings. It is gorgeous, the art is great, the sheriff token is very well done (and big) and the cloth bags are also very high quality (although the snaps can get damaged rather quickly I surmise). The game is very easy to explain, but it is a blast to play with the right game group. I love negotiation and bluffing games. Lots of laughs on this one. Also lots of luck, but this is a party/family game so I don’t care much about that. 

When I read the rules, I thought this game was very similar to Hart an der Grenze and Robin Hood, but I haven’t played either so I don’t know if they are similar or not. 

For now I want to play again and I will probably buy it. Good fun.

Current Rating: 6.5

RATING: 7
This is a good bluffing game and different than most of the others I have played in two main ways: When you bluff, it is immediately obvious (as soon as you store your cards). You can bluff all you want without consequence as long as you can convince others that it is in their best interest to not call you on it.

I have only played this once and would like to play again, but I am not stomping my feet to get it on the table with the gaming group(s). The main detraction for me and also for some others in my group is the scoring. Scoring is slow and arduous for such an otherwise light game. there is an app that can help, but it was not available when we played it. We will give it a try next time, but I expect it to only help some - you still have to count and log every card.

RATING: 7
Very group dependent as the game is in the player interaction. It needs players who are into bluffing, bribing and don't mind lying in a game. If players mostly play honest, don't trust anyone or simply cannot accept a bribe for not inspecting your bag when it's obvious by the amount of your bribe that your smuggling, play something else. Also, players need to haggle, threaten and talk shit for an enjoyable experience.

The cards of the first edition are of the weakest quality I have seen in a long time. The fake velvet bags are a fun component to play with although I wouldn't trust the button to withstand repeat plays. Better not close it at all in play.

I had fun with the game and would play again.  Some players in my group didn't feel to comfortable with the contraband and focused on the set collection aspect of the legal goods. Except me, nobody ever took contraband openly from the draw pile. I paid the highest bribes by far and in the end I probably had as much points from contraband as the other players together. Find out who is susceptive to bribes and use this opportunity for a joint profit. If there's nobody approachable at the table, forget it. Played as a mere set collection game it's a crapshoot of drawing the right cards.

RATING: 8
Very fun bluffing game that becomes really tense sometimes. When you are the sheriff you look people in the eye and try to read them. If you don't get a good bribe you might threaten people and see their reactions. The concept is quite brilliant. There is also mindgames you can do by taking cards from the middle but they are minor since your hand size is not that big. I also like the contraband version of the legal goods so that you can never be sure if you are actually winning. My only complaint is that the bags get ripped after a while but Arcane Wonders is such a wonderful company they sent replacements for all the bags plus they sent some promos along with it. Love the game and company.

RATING: 6.8
We all know the story of Robin Hood, but what if we could help him out a bit and smuggle goods into Nottingham past the no-good sheriff?! Well you can in this game but are you as good a liar as you think you are? You must smuggle as many goods as you can into Nottingham past the sheriff, aaahh yes you can bribe the sneaky no-good sheriff BUT will he look the other way or even believe your lies?! 
Each player takes turns being the sheriff until all have been sheriff once! So which of you are a no-good liar that should never be trusted and which of you are the lie detector?

Personal hangups aside, it is kind of fun especially when people are roleplaying a bit. I don't mind playing it once in awhile but there are many, many games that I would rather play instead. This will stay in my collection for the time being though as my son and some of his friends love it.

RATING: 6
Love the idea of this game on paper. Using deception, bluffing, mind games, and negotiation to win the game sounds awesome. A great theme and great artwork seem to make this game stand out. However, when actually playing, it usually  comes down to the most honest player winning, which goes against the whole idea of the game to me. The reward for smuggling contraband is not nearly enough, so in the end there is no real reason to. Table talk is the primary mechanic here, so if your group doesn't do well with role playing, this game will fall flat.

RATING: 7
A gateway game to more involved Bluffing/Negotiation Games.  I can't say that I was ever much a fan of bluffing games so that's probably why this game appeals even more to me.  It really is a beautiful production and the pouches work really well as a gimmick to conceal the cards yet also add a little thematic flair.  We've played mostly with 3 to date and it works just fine.  Our 8 year old son really loves the opportunity to "lie" and try to get away with stuff yet learn the lesson of what happens when you lie too much. 

I do like the way the set collection works here as well given the bonus for having the most of lower valued items is much higher than that for higher valued items by themselves.  The Royal Goods card are another nice addition to add just a little bit of variance and complexity.  It's a bit of a shame having to take all the bread out of the 3 player game as it reduces the variety in goods but I agree that this is what balances the 3 player game such that it plays the same as with the higher counts.

In our games thus far the negotiation element has failed slightly in that it almost always ends up as money being that which is offered and changes hands.  By the rules you can also offer up goods you already have, potential goods in your bag, or future favors.  It just hasn't yet seemed like any of those were much worthwhile though perhaps with more experience we will see the value in offering such over coin alone.

RATING: 7.5
Sheriff of Nottingham is a pretty tough game.. fun... but tough. If you dont have a good poker face, this might not be the best game for you. If you have a refined sense of telling lies, you might do pretty well. Basically, youre a merchant selling goods, but some of the goods you are selling might be contraband. Your job is to convince the Sheriff of Nottingham that all your goods are legal, even if they are not. His job is to sniff out the liars. Its played over a series of 2 rounds where everyone is the sheriff twice and then the gold is counted at then end.

RATING: N/A
In Sheriff of Nottingham, players will not only be able to experience Nottingham as a merchant of the city, but each turn one player will step into the shoes of the Sheriff himself. Players declare goods they wish to bring into the city, goods that are secretly stored in their burlap sack. The Sheriff must then determine who gets into the city with their goods, who gets inspected, and who may have their goods confiscated!

Do you have what it takes to be seen as an honest merchant? Will you make a deal with the Sheriff to let you in? Or will you persuade the Sheriff to target another player while you quietly slip by the gate? Declare your goods, negotiate deals, and be on the lookout for the Sheriff of Nottingham!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Rating this game is [b][i]very[/i][/b] dependent on the group you can play it with. My rating is based on my personal experience and by playing it with the right group of backstabbing, lying maniacs.

Otherwise, I can objectively see people ranking it lower. If all players are equally getting into the game, it's brilliant. Just make sure that nobody ever takes things too seriously.

The artworks are really gorgeous, the component quality is great. The cards are arguably a bit thin in comparison to most other games, but that's understandable, considering the huge amount of cards and production costs. Players need to be a bit careful with handling the bags though, as a too quick and rough opening can tear the thin cloth.
The most disappointing thing for me is that the game "only" supports up to 5 players, while [b][thing=22237]►Hart an der Grenze[/thing][/b] (which is the version I played before) supported up to 6 players.

Nevertheless, this is critique on a high level. Great game, [i][b]if[/b][/i] played with the right group of players.

RATING: 8
Ein sehr schönes Funspiel, bei dem es, zumindest mir, nicht ums Gewinnen geht. Man merkt auch deutlich, wer des Lügens nicht so fähig ist bzw. des Einschätzens der anderen Lügner ;).
In jeder Runde ist ein neuer Spieler der Sheriff und muss die anderen Spieler durchs Tor lassen und dabei ihre Waren kontrollieren. Die anderen Spieler stecken 1-5 ihrer 6 Handkarten in einen undurchsichtigen Beutel und schieben es dem Sheriff zu, wobei man die Anzahl und die Ware (nur eine einzige) deklarieren muss (Bsp.: ich habe hier 3 Äpfel). Dabei kann man dem Sheriff auch Bestechungsgelder, Waren und Versprechungen für zukünftige Runden anbieten. Öffnet der Sheriff den Beutel nicht, darf man alles darin behalten, egal ob dabei gelogen wurde oder nicht. Öffner er ihn allerdings, dann muss für jede falsch deklarierte Ware eine Strafe bezahlt werden (Schmuggelware dabei deutlich teurer, die darf auch nicht deklariert werden). Falls meine Angaben allerdings stimmten muss der Sheriff mir eine Strafe zahlen, da ich ja nicht gelogen habe...
Ein sehr schönes ich-denke-was-du-denkst Spiel... "Das sind 5 Äpfel" -> "Nie im Leben hast du 5 Äpfel" -> "Komm ich biete dir 3 Gold wenn du mich durchlässt" -> "Jetzt weiss ich dass dü lügst" *plopp+, der Beutel ist geöffnet und es kamen raus: 5 Äpfel... Strafe von 10 Gold! herrlich ;)
Mir gefällt das Spiel sehr gut, da man andere Spieler so hereinlegen kann, dabei sind mir Siegpunkte gar nicht so wichtig. Schön ist es wenn man einerseits die Wahrheit sagt und trotzdem Schmiergeld anbietet, wobei der Sheriff den Beutel öffnet. Eine Runde später beim gleichen Sheriff aber Schmuggelware von hohem Wert an ihm vorbeischmuggelt :)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This is another game that I believe will be an instant classic.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Call it Robin Hood because Prohis has made a fool out of the Sheriff of Nottingham. I'm just going to defer to myself last year when I said:


Things that Prohis does better: 
- It takes out the overcomplication of various types of goods that are pretty much on there for theme by making each good one of three things: legal goods (worth $1k in your warehouse), illegal goods ($4k in your warehouse, -$4k in your hand), and inspectors (ranging value based on strength. 
- The challenge process is substantially better. When someone tries to ship to their warehouse, each player bids on whether or not they want to inspect that shipment. You start the game with an equal number of inspectors with 1, 2, or 3 stars. The player to bid their highest inspector inspects that shipment, flipping over as many cards as stars on their inspector. If they hit contraband, they take the entire shipment, adding it to their warehouse. If they don't, they have to give their inspector to the other player. You can also bribe someone not to inspect you or bluff by saying "go ahead". I like this process better because everyone participates in the challenge process, and you have more options.
- I like the scoring better. I think there's too much randomness in Sheriff of Nottingham that's eliminated in Prohis because a) you can choose to draw face up cards or take off of the pile and b) scoring is consistent across legal vs nonlegal goods.

RATING: 9
For pure outrageous fun, this is one of the best games I have ever played. Having played it with total strangers as well as friends, I can say that -- if played correctly* -- you are guaranteed to enjoy the experience. 

The components are well constructed, the game has a simple flow, and the bluffing and negotiation are boundless sources of cheer. 

For most audiences*, this is a must-have. LOVE IT!!


* It's important to note that the enjoyment of this game is in direct proportion to how much the participants are willing to let go, unwind, play it up (bad British accents, etc), and get a bit goofy. If you or your gaming group are stuffed shirts or introverts, your mileage may vary.

RATING: 8
Played this at BGG con with a new group. There were 5 of us. It's definitely a fun game. Interestingly, I find that it's sort of difficult to bluff well in this one, even at 5 players. It seems like your best bet is to bid high (5 or more), if you can afford it, which forces the sheriff to potentially pay out big in order to search your bag. Low bids will (1-2) will most likely pass through, and medium bids (3-4) are the most likely to get checked. All in all, a solid game.

RATING: 9.5
2nd best game of 2014.
Strictly speaking it's not a 2014 game, but I had only heard about the original game and not played it so.. Re-themeing and re-targeting for wider audience does miracles. Wonderful components and easy rules (scoring is bit complex, BUT you don't really have to worry about that until the game ends so it's not a big deal). This isn't a game about winning (you can break the game if everyone plays honest, but that's the case with all hidden role games really), it belongs to same genre of smart partygames as Cash n' Guns for example, but just happens to look more like 'normal' eurogame. Great mix of negotiation and bluffing. Just great!

+GenCon Promo Cards

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
A light bluffing game about smuggling goods into Nottingham. What I like about this game is how it never requires you to lie, you can legitimately win by being honest the whole time. Players take turns being the Sheriff who may choose to inspect the goods of other players. Players may bribe the Sheriff to let them go or to inspect their bag or someone else's, if the Sheriff finds contraband it's confiscated and players have the pay a fine, if the Sheriff inspects a bag of legal goods they must pay the inspected player for the inconvenience. Whoever managed to accumulate the most wealth wins the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Sheriff of Nottingham is one of those social games that lives or dies on the player's willingness to engage in creative story telling and spinning a yarn. 

Each round the player assuming the role of the Sheriff must decide if the other players are being truthful in declaring what they are transporting in their bags. If a player is caught lying or falsely accused then cash will change hands as a consequence. But players can also offer a bribe to have the Sheriff look the other way and the Sheriff can even demand a payment to look the other way. 

What the players are trying to do is to get as many goods of various types (including lucrative contraband) past the Sheriff as it will score points at the end of the game. 

This game is about bluff and double bluff, spinning humorous yarns and hand management. Throw in some majority scoring and a few drinks and Sheriff of Nottingham is a great game to have in the collection for the right group and social situations. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
I usually like social deduction games, where you have to extract small clues and use them to convince the rest of the table. Sheriff of Nottingham has the tense balance between telling the truth (but make it seem like you're lying to get a compensation if checked) and bluffing (but make it seem like you're honest to get contraband past the sheriff). However, there are few clues given from the game but rather up to the players themselves to make up convincing stories. Also, the game in the game mainly takes places between the sheriff and only one other player, making the game less social. Players enjoying the role playing aspect may enjoy a game or two but I expect the replayability to be low.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Surprisingly blah.  The game can be really fun and funny, but I find that it's mostly just kind of boring.  Most of the time my group only tries to sneak contraband through once or twice a game, so the sheriff just keeps getting burned over and over again by opening bags.  If the sheriff tries to take their time questioning people, the game bogs down (EDIT: the app helps a lot with timing the sheriff, as well as helping with the tedious scoring!).

Great idea, just not as fun as I was hoping.  A hit with my group, however.

EDIT: Upgraded my rating based off some info I read here at BGG.  It basically said that as a bluffing game, Sheriff is pretty crappy.  As a NEGOTIATION game, however, it shines.  If you play to what the Sheriff is collecting (you see that he has a lot of apples, so you slip a few in your bag and offer him the choice of a card if he lets you through), the game becomes a LOT more fun and the amount of contraband trying to be brought in skyrockets, making all aspects of the game better.

RATING: 5
Yes, it's a bluffing/negotiation game, it's group dependent and you might like it more than I do, yada yada yada. The best thing I can say about Sheriff of Nottingham is that I would normally rate this game lower, but it has its moments. However, three problems:

- The amount of information you have to keep track of to be able to make semi-educated calls on any pouch's content is substantial. I do not rate the memory part of games highly, especially when the core gameplay decision wholly relies on it.
- Since any fine may set you back enough to be single-handedly game-losing, the game discourages boldness from both sheriff and merchants, which means that the least flamboyant half of your group will probably play a very uneventful and low involvement game.
- For how casual player friendly the core gameplay is, the lengthy maths operation we get in place of a readable scoring system seems completely inappropriate.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6

The high-risk high-reward method of smuggling sometimes pays off, but often you end up losing a huge amount more, whereas the slow and steady 'honesty policy' seems to be a far more effective way to victory. That said, it's great fun trying to deceive whoever is playing the sheriff, so maybe the secret is to just not worry too much about winning!

They are not necessary for the game, but they created an anxious feeling whenever you heard the click of the button when the Sheriff was about to open your bad and find illegal merchandise...

The rules are very simple: it’s a game about bluffing and trying to guess your opponents’ bluffs. For me, it provides an experience very similar to [thing=45]Liar's Dice[/thing], but it’s been upgraded components and most important, a theme that can inspire players to represent their roles and negotiate bribes. It’s one of those games that really depends on the players to provide the fun.

There’s a couple of things I didn’t like:
· I think it’s too long. It’s too much time doing the same thing. It’s not a big deal, though, because you can just stop after the first round and cut the duration in half.
· Why majorities are scored at the end? I think it serves no purpose, it just adds more uncontrolled randomness and unnecessary complexity.

It’s not a game I would like to play constantly, but it can be fun occasionally, when the players are right. And on top of it, you can also play it with your family or other non gamers, provided they are up for the challenge.

規則:
*起始形成兩疊各五張的棄牌推，每個人50圓，六張牌
*三人9輪，四人以上，人數*2輪
*每輪五個階段，每個階段每個人輪流做事，審查階段則同時
A 市場，蓋著最多五張牌在旁邊，然後補牌到六張，一定要先抽棄牌推，才能抽牌庫，棄牌推要照順序抽，將蓋著的牌一起放到某個棄牌推，順序隨便
B 放牌到袋中，一到五張
C 宣告你袋中貨物，只能宣告一種合法貨物，張數要對
D 警長審查，可用各種貨物賄絡(錢，送完的卡，袋中物品，未來承諾)，過的話，合法卡打開放置，違禁品蓋著放上面，如果檢視，你說實話警長要陪你懲罰的錢，說謊的話，有說的合法貨物依舊得到，違法或沒說的警長選棄牌推丟，你要付罰鍰給警長
E 補手牌到六張
*卡牌全用完則除了棄牌推上面五張，其它重洗
*最後記分可以先記物品擁有最多的第一第二額外分數，在各別記所有物品分數跟錢
*變體 手牌上限七張，起始移掉10張牌

RATING: 9.5
One of the best 5-player games ever. Perfect for any skill level of gamers and always livens up game days. The optimum strategy is to never lie and carry the most "allowed" goods but I like that the game almost forces you to change your strategy in every turn. The gameplay is short, sweet and easy to make decisions. The artwork is fantastic and fits with the theme. While the components could use a little help (the cards could be built of sturdier stock, the coins fall apart, and the bags tear where the snap is), Sheriff of Nottingham is a wonderful game to bring everyone back to life after a day of gaming or to show people new to gaming. One of the best bluffing games out now.

RATING: 6

RATING: 5
Sheriff of Nottingham is a set-collection game that revolves around negotiation, often in bad faith.  Basically, players rotate taking the role of the sheriff, and other players must declare what they're taking into the village (truthfully or not).  The sheriff has the opportunity to inspect one player's lot, and can take bribes from players to help influence his decision.  Personally, lying and extortion are not at all fun for me, so I didn't enjoy this one.

RATING: 7.6
This is an excellent party game. I highly recommend playing this with a bit of light (to medium) roleplaying. Get into character and try and bluff your way to victory.

This game actually requires a lot of skill. You need to be conniving and ruthless. You need to establish yourself as an honest merchant, then ruthlessly take advantage of everyone's trust. If you've ever wondered what it's like to be a cop conducting an interrogation, this is the game for you. You need to read everyone's facial expressions and body language, and determine if they're lying or not.

RATING: 8
A bluffing game in which the players each take a turn being the Sheriff of Nottingham. The object of the game is to gain the most gold (VP) at the end of the game. In order to do that, you must get your items to the Market by passing them through the Sheriff without inspection. Some items are legal, while some are illegal contraband. Lying, bribery, deal making are all essential part of this game. This is a great fun game to play with friends. Highly recommended. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A fun and flexible bluffing/bribing game. I like how many ways you can approach it: You can take the moderate honest reward or try for a higher, riskier reward. You can try to fool the sheriff into allowing your contraband through or you can straight-up bribe them to let it through. You can bribe the sheriff to not let someone else's shipment through if you think they're far in the lead.

Being the sheriff is a lot of fun too. It's a fun position of power where everyone's fates depend on your decisions for that round, and it can be fun to roleplay it and try to extort your friends.

The only real thing I don't like about it is how long it takes to play. At heart, it's a simple bluffing game with a fair amount of luck thrown in, and that type of game works best for me if it ends quickly so I don't feel annoyed by getting badly hurt from bad luck.

RATING: N/A
People complain that there's a degenerate strategy in this one (always tell the truth), then they blame the player(s) pursuing that strategy as "not playing the game." I don't buy it, and I think if you've designed a bluffing game where bluffing is a bad idea, then you're not quite done tweaking the game. 

Kakerlakenpoker is way, way, way better than this. SoN's truth-telling problem is sort of encouraged by the fact that there's one winner. Kakerlakenpoker dispenses with that and instead makes one [i]loser[/i], the rest winners. So SoN's problem is that the stated winning condition incentivizes players to do the very thing that makes the game unfun. This is not the players' fault at all. 

Ultimately, though, this is a simple set collection game turned into a much longer game for no real reason. Kakerlakenpoker is smaller, cheaper, faster to play, easier to explain, and doesn't suffer from a degenerate strategy. If all you're doing is collecting sets of things to then run through a triangular scoring table, why put up with much bother?

RATING: 2
Some people love this game and based on the ratings and reviews, I'm clearly in the minority.

Originally thought I didn't like this game because it was a bluffing games. This is not the case. I like Mafia, One Night, and Secret Hitler. So, I have no issue with bluffing games.

The reason this game is bad is two fold. First, no matter what, it's really just a guessing game. You don't accumulate knowledge throughout the game and work logic to see who is bluffing. Every round is new info. This makes it a random guess each round. The second issue is that the easiest way to win is to just not bluff. The penalty for bluffing is harsh and the penalty on the sheriff for calling out a non bluff is also harsh. There's no benefit to bluffing.

The game is not good and the hype is lost on me. My only guess is that sales are boosted by an excellent tabletop episode.

RATING: 6
Sheriff is essentially the board game evolution of the traditional card game "Bullshit"/"Cheat".

It's a wonderful way to spend an hour or so lying to your friends without the stress, hostility, or complication of games like Werewolf or Resistance.

It's clever, but doesn't offer much variety.  You may get tired of it after a few plays.

RATING: 8
Sheriff of Nottingham is fantastic.  It drew a crowd of spectators when I played it at my game club for the first time.  We had a blast, getting into the role-playing, bluffing, bribing and backstabbing!

What REALLY blew my mind though is this is the first game that my wife, son and I truly love! In my collection of close to 400 games, probably about 100 of them are family games, or games I bought with my family in mind.  Out of all of those games, there are quite a few that two out of the three of us love, but the third doesn't like it or think's it's just okay. There are some that only one of us love and the other two think it's just okay.  There are some that we all agree are kind of meh.  I was beginning to think I would never find a game that my wife, son and I all love to play.  Well, thanks to Arcane Wonders, I've finally found it!

RATING: 5

Namely, it is the means by which this game allows you to straight-faced LIE to your friends and family that gives it such novelty. However, a recent play revealed to me that this game wasn't all that it was once cracked up to be, or that my tastes in gaming have changed. It is likely the latter. I would in almost all scenarios play something less fiddly, less reliant on gimmicks, and more streamlined if I were to choose a bluffing game. Oh, say, Liar's Dice. Sheriff of Nottingham will still find a place in many a family/friend group--it's just that when Liar's Dice is just as accessible and all-the-more skill-related, why would I choose otherwise?

RATING: 6
I had high expectations from good recommendations, and I usually like bluffing games with imperfect hard evidence.  I was underwhelmed with the 3 player game, but I think it will probably be better with more.

The cards removed for 3 player games remove variety from the deck, changing the distribution from larger games.  It becomes more viable to draw a hand of 4-5 legitimate goods, making the game less about lying and more about just rummy-style draws.  That in turn makes inspections less about reading people and more about luck.  Overall, the game was flat.

I still have high hopes it will be better with more players and the full deck.  In fact, I see no reason why the full deck can't (and shouldn't) be used for 3 player games.

update:  with 5 players, the lying is much more fun, but the scoring is a bit less satisfying and arbitrary,  A net gain for a game that is all about lying.

RATING: 8
19-12-2014. Rated after 1 play. One of Tom Vasel's favorite games. Did I like it? Yeah. I did. But why?

First off, you are a merchant trying to make the most money in Nottingham. How do you do this? You of course get in trade goods. Legal ones are no problem, but those illegal goods might make it worthwhile..

In the game, you collect a hand of cards. You can discard up to five to draw new cards. The cards you discard are open, as potentially the cards you draw. You can draw from open discard piles or from the top of a deck. Then you put cards in a bag, these goods can be legal (green) or illegal (red bordered). 

You CAN lie about what is in your bag, but not about the number of cards you put in. If the sheriff opens your bag, you have to pay fines if you tried to snuck in illegal goods. If you didn't, the sheriff needs to pay you for his transgressions and corruption.

The game is fun, but highly group dependent. So make sure that the group you play with likes roleplaying/backstabbing/cheating. If you play with the wrong group this game breaks down. I am not so impressed about the components. The cards and art is good, but the cardboard tokens / boards are a little less than I have come to expect with tearing tokens and misprinted/ uncentered boards.

RATING: 8
I have only played this game once so far, but am looking forward to future plays. It was just the right level of complexity for our group (it may be a bit too complex for a social game night with all non-gamers, as the rules did take a bit of time to get through, but it was just the right complexity level for our group of "moderate gamers"). 

To be honest, this is the type of game I would have probably walked right past at a store (we received it as a gift), assuming it to be a bit too rule-heavy and fantasy-oriented in nature for our typical crowd, but the core gameplay is actually quite straightforward once you get through the basic rules.

Pros:
-Nice mix of bluffing / strategy / luck. I found that framing the game in the context of the familiar BS / Cheat card game made its general concept more immediately accessible to the group.
-High quality game, everything feels really sturdy
-You can customize the cards in the deck to suit your needs (e.g. reducing to a 3 person game, upping the challenge by putting in the Royal Goods cards, etc.)
-It seemed like there were additional ways we could strategize as we got more familiar with the game, which makes me think that we will continue to find good replay value with this game.
-The "king of X" bonuses as the end added another level of strategy to the game (sort of like the "longest route" bonus in Ticket to Ride)

Cons:
-To echo what others have said, I can see how the game may not incentivize aggressive bluffing enough. One person in our group who played a completely honest game ended up coming in as a very close second. I like the idea of adding in the Royal Goods as a way to potentially address this challenge.
-May be a bit off-putting to non-gamers at first, but hopefully a quick run-through of the basic premise will make it clear that the game is actually not so complicated after all.
-This is a small nuance, but we found the card tray to be annoying, as it made it difficult to dig under the top card on the discard pile to see what was underneath. We quickly remedied this by just putting the card piles directly on the table.
-We'd like to see some more examples of the bribing element in live play, to get a better sense off how this can play out effectively - we used bribing to some extent, but it felt like we left some of the potential untapped here (there wasn't a lot of back-and-forth negotiation in our group).

Overall, this seems like a gem of a game, and I'm surprised that it took us this long to find out about it!

RATING: 5
Ditches the tin suitcases of Hart an der Grenze and adopts the little pouches that came with Robin Hood. It's the third or fourth incarnation of the 1950 game Contraband, with all new artwork, but it plays pretty much the same. Barely rates a new entry here on BGG.

Takes the whimsical border smuggling of Hart an der Grenze and gives it a spin in Sherwood Forest tying to smuggle your wares past the Sheriff of Nottingham. 

A few deals are struck, lots of risk taking, bluffing and guessing and not much else. Repeat the same thing over several rounds and you end up with a winner.

It's okay, but not a game I feel the inclination to keep bringing to the table. More of a social experience with disbelief at what players will try and get past you with an innocent look on their faces. Worth a laugh, but there's better laughs out there.

RATING: 9
This is an intense game of bluffing with numerous possibilities for optimizing profits. Getting people to think you've lied when you haven't, paying off the sheriff to open someone else's bag instead of your own; there are so many ways to play this game.

My only complaint with Sheriff of Nottingham is that, most of the time, crime doesn't seem to pay. I find myself winning most often by being an honest merchant, and that's honestly not a lot of fun. I think that either the bonuses should be reduced or contraband should be worth a lot more.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I've played Sherriff three times at this time, and every time has been good, uproarious fun. Admittedly, much of the fun is gleaned by how "dirty" the players are playing (honest players will almost certainly fail in this game) as well as how much they're roleplaying. I'd recommend that the group's ambassador compels the group to do funny voices, and play as funny characters to spice things up and encourage sleazier dealings... The screams of my group as I put 4 items into my contraband pile after only bribing the sheriff $7 is pretty priceless.

SPOILERS for some basic strategy: Basically, your goal in this game is to get as many items to market as possible, legal or otherwise. A smart player should be open-handed (to a point) with bribes. I mention this in the review because it's important to point out to new players that playing honestly will not be a winning strategy.

RATING: 5.5
It's a smuggling game - you're merchants bringing stuff across the border (or in this version into a city), declaring what's in your bag and having trouble if the inspection finds anything you didn't claim to be there. However the inspector (sheriff) has a problem, if they open a bag and everything is legal. You can bribe the sheriff offering them money, delivered goods, potential goods (ha!) - to not check your bag, or maybe somebody else's, or whatever you wish. The trick is that any deal made for the current round is binding. This lays down the framework for a player driven hilarious game about bluffing and negotiating (kinda sorta). And as with best games of this type the groupthink grows with the game and the group. Anybody claiming to find "optimal strategies" is just formulating their groupthink that can be countered. You just need to reach that equilibrium where you're not sure if a certain move is honest, a bluff, a counter-bluff or a counter-counter-bluff. Light roleplaying helps, I mean, it's an excuse to do stupid things before other player's noses. 

I'll try to get over the hideous front cover art, will see if I'll manage. Oh and the theme is pretty pedestrian as well.

RATING: 5
Playing this game was fun. I'm sure it's the kind of game that can be random and overly long with the wrong group, but it can be a hoot with people who spend more time thinking about the theme than the math. Of course, it's not much of a challenge to win against the latter compared to the former. In my play, I quickly concluded that an overall strategy of set collecting legal goods, making it look like I was lying while telling the truth, and lying big when I didn't have a useful hand, with a bribe if necessary, was likely to yield the best return. It did and I won. The others weren't thinking about the game the way I was. That was good for the experience, and it helped me win, but it's not promising for long term replayability. Once everyone realizes how the game works, I think it will devolve into a guessing game. This game is a bit like Poker, but it's much less mathematically interesting. The fun of the game--the bluffing--can be had in less time and with much less overhead with Cockroach Poker.
